Plato's Meno

Geoffrey Steadman

70a1ΜΕΝ. ἔχεις μοι εἰπεῖν, ὦ Σώκρατες, ἆρα διδακτὸν ἡ
70a2ἀρετή; ἢ οὐ διδακτὸν ἀλλ᾽ ἀσκητόν; ἢ οὔτε ἀσκητὸν οὔτε
70a3μαθητόν, ἀλλὰ φύσει παραγίγνεται τοῖς ἀνθρώποις ἢ ἄλλῳ
70a4τινὶ τρόπῳ;
70a5ΣΩ. ὦ Μένων, πρὸ τοῦ μὲν Θετταλοὶ εὐδόκιμοι ἦσαν
70a6ἐν τοῖς Ἕλλησιν καὶ ἐθαυμάζοντο ἐφ᾽ ἱππικῇ τε καὶ πλούτῳ,
70b1νῦν δέ, ὡς ἐμοὶ δοκεῖ, καὶ ἐπὶ σοφίᾳ, καὶ οὐχ ἥκιστα οἱ τοῦ
70b2σοῦ ἑταίρου Ἀριστίππου πολῖται Λαρισαῖοι. τούτου δὲ ὑμῖν
70b3αἴτιός ἐστι Γοργίας· ἀφικόμενος γὰρ εἰς τὴν πόλιν ἐραστὰς
70b4ἐπὶ σοφίᾳ εἴληφεν Ἀλευαδῶν τε τοὺς πρώτους, ὧν ὁ σὸς

Commentary

70a1ἡ ἀρετή (ἐστιν) add a linking verb
70a1ἔχεις are you able…?; + inf.
70a1ἆρα whether…; indirect question
70a2ἡ ἀρετή (ἐστιν) add a linking verb
70a2διδακτὸν…ἀσκητόν see the grammar box below
70a3φύσει by…; φύσε-ι, dat. of means, φύσις
70a3τοῖς ἀνθρώποις to…; dative of compound verb
70a5τοῦ this (time); translate as demonstrative
70a5(οἱ) Θετταλοί Attic authors often omit the article for national groups
70a5ἦσαν imperfect εἰμί
70a6ἐθαυμάζοντο passive
70a6ἐφ᾽... for…; ἐπί...; a dative of cause with a verb of emotion (S1517) may sometimes be preceded by ἐπί (S1689c)
70b1ὡς... as…; a parenthetical clause
70b1καί also; adverb
70b1ἐπὶ... dative of cause, see above
70b1ἥκιστα superlative adverb is often, as here, an adverbial accusative in the neuter plural
70b2πολῖται (fellow)-citizens; assume a form of θαυμάζω as the verb
70b2τούτου for…; genitive of charge with αἴτιος (S1425, S1375)
70b2ὑμῖν for you all; i.e. for Meno and his fellow Thessalians; dative of interest
70b3ἐραστάς as lovers
70b4ἐπὶ... see above; take closely with ἐραστάς
70b4εἴληφεν 3s perfect λαμβάνω
70b4τοὺς πρώτους i.e. the leading men
70b4ὧν among…; relative pronoun and partitive genitive

Commentary

70b5καὶ δὴ καί and in particular; ‘and indeed also,’ the second καί is an adverb (S2890)
70b6καὶ δὴ καί and in particular; ‘and indeed also,’ the second καί is an adverb (S2890)
70b6ἀφόβως...ἀποκρίνεσθαι... (namely) that (they)…; indirect discourse with missing accusative subject
70b6εἴθικεν he has made…accustomed to this custom; 3s perfect ἐθίζω; Gorgias is the subject; τοῦτο τὸ ἔθος is a cognate accusative
70b7τοὺς εἰδότας (ἀποκρίνεσθαι) that those…; indirect discourse with accusative plural participle οἶδα
70b7ἀφόβως...ἀποκρίνεσθαι... (namely) that (they)…; indirect discourse with missing accusative subject
70b7ἐὰν...ἔρηται a present general condition (ἐάν + subjunctive, present) with middle subjunctive ἔρομαι; τίς is indefinite τις
70b7εἰκός (ἐστιν) (it is)…; impersonal, add verb
70c1τοὺς εἰδότας (ἀποκρίνεσθαι) that those…; indirect discourse with accusative plural participle οἶδα
70c1ἅτε...παρέχων inasmuch as…; or ‘since,’ ἅτε + participle indicates a cause from the speaker’s point of view
70c1καί in fact, actually; adverb
70c1(ἑ)αυτὸν note accent; 3rd person reflexive
70c1ἐρωτᾶν for questioning; ‘to be questioned’; an epexegetical (explanatory) infinitive is often active in Greek where English prefers the passive (S2006); present alpha-contract infinitive
70c2τῷ βουλομένῳ (ἐρωτᾶν) to (anyone)…
70c2ὅ τι ἂν... whatever…; general relative clause, neuter singular ὅστις (ὅ τι is equivalent to ὅτι)
70c2οὐδενὶ ὅτῳ οὐκ to anyone whosoever; ‘to no one who not;’ dative ὅστις; see S2534
70c3ἐνθάδε δέ i.e. in Athens
70c4περιέστηκεν, γέγονεν 3s perfect, γίγνομαι
71a1κινδυνεύει...οἴχεσθαι runs the risk of having gone…, is likely to have gone…
71a1παρ(ὰ)... to…; accusative place to which
71a2τῶν ἐνθάδε of those here; partitive genitive
71a2οὐδεὶς ὅστις οὐ everyone; ‘(there is) no one who not,’ treat as one pronoun (S2534)
71a3ἐρεῖ future λέγω (ἐρέω)
71a4ἀρετὴν...εἰδέναι (namely) to know whether virtue (is)…; ‘to know virtue whether…’; proleptic use of ἀρετήν; infinitive οἶδα
71a4ὅτῳ τρόπῳ in whatever way; dative ὅστις

Commentary

71a5ἀρετὴν...εἰδέναι (namely) to know whether virtue (is)…; ‘to know virtue whether…’; proleptic use of ἀρετήν; infinitive οἶδα
71a5τοσοῦτον δέω I am far from + infinitive; ‘I lack so much from;’ adverbial accusative (inner accusative)
71a5εἴτε...εἴτε... whether (it is)…or…; add verb
71a6ὅ τι ποτ(ε) ἐστὶ...ἀρετή what in the world...; indirect question with neuter ὅστις; a common idiom with ποτε (S346)
71a6οὐδέ not even; adverb, not conjunction
71a6τὸ παράπαν adverb, often with article
71a7ὅ τι ποτ(ε) ἐστὶ...ἀρετή what in the world...; indirect question with neuter ὅστις; a common idiom with ποτε (S346)
71a7τυγχάνω εἰδώς happen to…; τυγχάνω + complementary participle; nominative singular perfect participle οἶδα
71b1καί too, also; adverb
71b1οὕτως ἔχω I am…; ἔχω (‘is disposed’ or ‘holds’) + adverb is often equivalent to εἰμί + adjective
71b2τοῖς πολίταις with…; dative of compound
71b2τούτου πράγματος in…; a genitive of separation with a verb of need/lack (S1396)
71b3ὡς...εἰδώς on the grounds that…; ‘since...’; ὡς + participle expresses alleged cause
71b3ὃ δὲ...ἐστιν (that) which...; (τοῦτο) ὃ…: Greek often omits an antecedent of a relative clause if it is a demonstrative; that missing τοῦτο is either (1) an accusative of respect or (2) the subject of τί ἐστιν used proleptically as object of οἶδα; μή indicates that the clause is conditional in sense
71b4ὃ δὲ...ἐστιν (that) which...; (τοῦτο) ὃ…: Greek often omits an antecedent of a relative clause if it is a demonstrative; that missing τοῦτο is either (1) an accusative of respect or (2) the subject of τί ἐστιν used proleptically as object of οἶδα; μή indicates that the clause is conditional in sense
71b4ἂν...εἰδείην would…; 1s potential optative οἶδα
71b4ὁποῖόν γέ (ἐστιν) τι what sort at all (it is); indirect question; τις, τι often follow pronouns, often to add emphasis (S1268)
71b4ἢ δοκεῖ or does it…; a question
71b5οἷόν τε εἶναι to be possible; ‘to be the sort to;’ οἷός τε εἰμί + infinitive is a common idiom for ‘to be able’ or ‘to be possible’
71b5ὅστις... τοῦτον is antecedent; μή, see b3
71b6τοῦτον εἰδέναι that this one…; indirect discourse, infinitive οἶδα governed by οἷόν τε εἶναι
71b6καί in fact, actually; adverb, here and in line 7
71b7τὰ (ἐ)ναντία adverbial accusative
71b9ἔμοι-γε dative ἔγωγε
71c1οὐδὲ ὅ τι not even what…; adverbial οὐδέ
71c2ἀπαγγέλλωμεν are we to…?; deliberative subjunctive; καί ‘also’ modifies the verb

78d8τούτῳ τῷ πόρῳ to this procuring; dative of compound verb προσ-εῖναι.

78e3τὸ δὲ μὴ ἐκπορίζειν... not procuring; the articular infinitive is the subject and is conditional in sense; add ἐστίν in the main clause.
78e4τὸ δὲ μὴ ἐκπορίζειν... not procuring; the articular infinitive is the subject and is conditional in sense; add ἐστίν in the main clause.

78e5αὑτῷ for oneself; (ἑ)αυτῷ; dative of interest with the articular infinitive.
78e5ἀπορία lack of resources; compare 72a2, where the same word refers to perplexity or bewilderment.
78e6οὐδέν not at all; adverbial accusative modifying a comparative.
78e7ἂν εἴη 3s potential optative εἰμί.
78e8ὃ μὲν...γίγνηται,...ἔσται whatever…; general relative clause and future εἰμί, equivalent to a future more vivid condition.

Commentary

93e9Δία Accusative of Ζεύς in oath formula.
93e10μὲν δή “Certainly”; expresses positive certainty in conclusions (S2900).
93e10σοι Either dative of interest or ethical dative to engage the addressee: “you know.”
93e10τοιοῦτος (ἦν) Predicate: “was this sort of.”
93e11ἐν τοῖς ἄριστον “Best among this sort,” or “among the best.”
93e11τῶν προτέρων Previous generations.
94a1δὲ δή “But now”; transition to a new point (S2839).
94a1σκεψώμεθα First plural hortatory subjunctive: “let us consider.”
94a1τὸν Λυσιμάχου “Son of Lysimachus.”
94a2γεγονέναι Perfect active infinitive; translate as “was / has proved to be.”
94a4οὗτος Refers to Aristides.
94a4τὸν ὑὸν τὸν αὑτοῦ Λυσίμαχον Greeks often named a son after the father’s father; this Lysimachus is Aristides’ son.
94a5ὅσα “All things in which…”; relative and accusative of respect, with missing antecedent as object.
94a5εἴχετο “Depended on”; literally “clung to” + partitive genitive.
94a5κάλλιστα Superlative adverb of καλῶς.
94a5ἐπαίδευσε Governs a double accusative.
94a6βελτίονα Third-declension accusative.
94a6ὁτουοῦν Genitive of comparison; alternative form for οὗτινος-οῦν.
94a7καὶ συγγέγονας “You actually have associated”; second singular perfect.
94a7βούλει βούλε(σ)αι, second singular present middle.
94b2ἔθρεψε Aorist of τρέφω.
94b4ἐδίδαξεν δίδασκω with double accusative; cf. 92d2.

Commentary

94d3οὗ δὲ...ταῦτα δὲ “But those things where it was not necessary to make them good men by paying…”; οὗ is a relative adverb.
94d3(ἄν) ἐδίδαξεν Supply ἄν from the previous construction: “would have taught”; see the previous note on 94c7.
94d3εἰ...ἦν If it were…; a mixed contrary-to-fact condition (εἰ imperfect, ἄν + aorist). Socrates asks why Thucydides taught other skills but failed to make his sons good men if virtue is teachable.
94d3ἀλλὰ γάρ “But…”; here introduces an imaginary objection. The γάρ explains the response to the preceding question, while ἀλλά marks an objection to a negative statement.
94d4αὐτῷ Dative of possession: “he had.”
94d5καὶ οἰκίας...ἐπιμέλειαν καί is adversative, similar to καίτοι; the phrase continues the reply to the imaginary objection.
94d5οἰκίας μεγάλης Genitive of quality as predicate: “of a great house.”
94d6ἐδύνατο μέγα Idiom: “had great influence.”
94d6ὥστε Result clause with infinitive: “so that…”
94d7εἴπερ ἦν, ἐξευρεῖν ἂν Mixed contrary-to-fact condition: if it were, he would have found; aorist infinitive ἐξευρίσκω.
94d7τοῦτο Refers to ἀρετή; subject of the condition.
94d7ὅστις Someone who…; the relative clause has an antecedent that is the object of ἐξευρεῖν.
94d7ἔμελλεν μέλλω often governs a future infinitive.
94e2ἀλλὰ γάρ Marks the unfulfillment of the condition: “but / no, for on the contrary…”
94e2μὴ οὐκ ᾖ διδακτόν ἀρετή Doubtful assertion/denial: “I suspect virtue is not teachable”; μή/μὴ οὐ + present subjunctive (S1801).
94e3κακῶς λέγειν To speak poorly about someone.
94e4μὲν οὖν Certainly; affirmative particle combination.
94e4ἂν συμβουλεύσαιμι First singular aorist potential optative.
94e5ὡς...πάνυ Introduces a long comparative clause; καί means “also.”

Known issues in this text

Text and commentary were digitised by OCR, anchored to individual words by a neural pass, then post-processed. These are the measured artefacts of that pipeline — the commentary itself is unaltered.

Notes
2,225
Anchored to a line, not a word
55 · 1.6% — the neural pass could not match the editor's citation form to a word in the text; these open from the line number
Phrases only partly anchored
173 — a multi-word phrase where not every word is underlined, usually one broken across a line
